Base directory for this skill: /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/.claude/skills/documentation-style

# Documentation Styling Rules

This skill enforces comprehensive documentation standards across all projects.

## Critical Rules

### 1. NO LINE ART - EVER
**ABSOLUTE RULE**: Never create ASCII art or line-based diagrams in documentation.

**ALWAYS USE**:
- PlantUML for architecture diagrams, sequence diagrams, component diagrams
- Mermaid for flowcharts, state diagrams, simple visualizations

**WHY**: Text-based "line art" is not accessible, difficult to maintain, and looks unprofessional.

### 2. PlantUML Diagram Standards

**Location**: All PlantUML files MUST be stored in `docs/puml/`

**Style Sheet**: ALWAYS include the standard style sheet from coding project as the FIRST line after the opening tag.

**Layout Guidelines**:
- **Standard diagrams**: Prefer VERTICAL layouts to avoid excessive width
- Reason: Prevents users from zooming and scrolling horizontally
- Vertical scrolling is acceptable and preferred over horizontal scrolling
- Aim for narrow, tall diagrams that fit within typical screen widths

**Workflow for Creating PlantUML Diagrams**:

1. **Create the .puml file** in `docs/puml/` with proper naming
2. **Include standard style** - see reference documentation for the exact include syntax
3. **Design with vertical layout** - stack components top-to-bottom when possible
4. **Validate syntax** by attempting to render with plantuml checkonly flag
5. **Fix any errors** reported by plantuml validation
6. **Generate PNG** once error-free using plantuml command
7. **Move PNG to images folder** in docs/images/
8. **Reference in markdown** using relative path to the image

**IMPORTANT**: Never claim success until you've verified the PNG was created without errors.

### 3. Filename Conventions

**STRICT RULES** for ALL documentation artifacts (`.md`, `.puml`, `.png`, etc.):

**Permitted characters**:
- Lowercase letters: `a-z`
- Hyphens: `-`
- Numbers: `0-9`
- Extensions: `.md`, `.puml`, `.png`, etc.

**ONLY permitted exception**: `README.md` (capital letters allowed)

**Good Examples**:
- `system-architecture.puml`
- `deployment-flow.md`
- `api-endpoints.png`
- `README.md` (exception)

**Bad Examples**:
- Capital letters in names
- Underscores instead of hyphens
- CamelCase or PascalCase naming

### 4. NO INCREMENTAL NAMING

**CRITICAL**: Filenames and diagram text MUST represent the CURRENT STATE only, never showing evolution.

**FORBIDDEN PATTERNS** - Never use these suffixes or words:
- Version numbers or indicators
- Words suggesting improvement or change
- Words suggesting temporary status
- Words suggesting alternatives

**Why**: Documentation should reflect current state, not history. Use git for version history.

**Always**: Update the original file directly instead of creating variants.

### 5. Diagram Text Content

Text WITHIN diagrams must also be non-incremental:
- Component names should be simple and current
- Node labels should not indicate versions
- Actor names should not suggest enhancement status

## Implementation Checklist

When creating or updating documentation, verify:

- [ ] No ASCII/line art used (use PlantUML or Mermaid)
- [ ] PlantUML files stored in `docs/puml/`
- [ ] Standard style sheet included in .puml files
- [ ] PlantUML syntax validated with plantuml checkonly
- [ ] PNG generated successfully with plantuml
- [ ] PNG moved to `docs/images/`
- [ ] All filenames use lowercase + hyphens only (except README.md)
- [ ] No incremental suffixes in filenames
- [ ] No incremental labels in diagram text
- [ ] Markdown properly references images from `docs/images/`

## Tool Requirements

**Required tool**: `plantuml` must be installed on the system.

**Verification**:
```bash
which plantuml || echo "ERROR: plantuml not installed"
```

## Error Recovery

If PlantUML generation fails:

1. **Read the error message carefully** - PlantUML errors are usually specific
2. **Check syntax** - common issues include missing tags, unclosed quotes, invalid stereotypes, incorrect arrow syntax
3. **Validate include path** - ensure style sheet path is correct
4. **Test incrementally** - comment out sections to isolate problems

## Project-Specific Paths

### Standard Mode Style Sheet
Located at: `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/docs/puml/_standard-style.puml`

Use this path for regular documentation diagrams (12pt fonts, 2pt lines, vertical layout preference).

### Presentation Mode Style Sheet
Located at: `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/docs/presentation/puml/_standard-style.puml`

Use this path for presentation diagrams (18pt fonts, 3-4pt lines, horizontal layout preference).

**IMPORTANT**: Both style sheets are named `_standard-style.puml` but are in different directories. The constraint monitor requires all PlantUML files to include a file named `_standard-style.puml`, so we use the same name in both locations but with different content optimized for each use case.

## PRESENTATION MODE

### When to Use Presentation Mode

Create a presentation mode version when:
- User explicitly requests "presentation mode" or "PPT version"
- Diagram will be used in PowerPoint or similar presentation software
- Diagram needs to be readable from distance (projector/large screen)
- Focus should be on key concepts, not detailed annotations

### Presentation Mode Workflow

When asked to create a presentation mode version:

1. **Copy source file** from `docs/puml/` to `coding/docs/presentation/puml/`
   - Keep the same filename (no suffix changes)
   - This is stored in coding project for reuse across all projects

2. **Rework the diagram** with these changes:
   - **Thicker lines**: All connections and borders become more prominent
   - **Increased font size**: All text becomes larger (18pt vs 12pt)
   - **Essential text only**: Remove verbose labels, keep only critical identifiers
   - **Remove annotations**: Delete all notes, legends, and explanatory text
   - **Horizontal layout**: Arrange for landscape PPT slide (left-to-right flow)
   - **Simplify**: Focus on core concepts, remove implementation details

3. **Update style sheet include** to presentation style:

   **Absolute path** (when referencing from any project):
   ```
   !include /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/docs/presentation/puml/_standard-style.puml
   ```

   **Relative path** (when file is in the presentation/puml directory):
   ```
   !include _standard-style.puml
   ```

   Note: This is a different `_standard-style.puml` than the regular one - it's the presentation mode version with larger fonts and thicker lines.

4. **Validate and generate**:
   ```bash
   plantuml -checkonly coding/docs/presentation/puml/diagram-name.puml
   plantuml coding/docs/presentation/puml/diagram-name.puml
   mv coding/docs/presentation/puml/diagram-name.png coding/docs/presentation/images/
   ```

5. **Verify** the presentation PNG is created and suitable for PPT use

### Presentation Mode Characteristics

**Differences from Standard Mode**:

| Aspect | Standard Mode | Presentation Mode |
|--------|--------------|-------------------|
| Layout | Vertical (narrow, tall) | Horizontal (wide, landscape) |
| Font Size | 12pt | 18pt |
| Line Thickness | 2pt | 3-4pt |
| Text Detail | Comprehensive | Essential only |
| Annotations | Included | Removed |
| Notes/Legends | Present | Omitted |
| Purpose | Documentation | Presentation |
| Location | `docs/puml/` | `coding/docs/presentation/puml/` |

**Visual Optimization**:
- Thicker borders make elements visible from distance
- Larger fonts readable on projectors
- Horizontal layout fits 16:9 or 4:3 PPT slides
- Minimal text reduces cognitive load
- No legends/notes - slides should be self-explanatory or presenter explains

### Presentation Mode Example

**Original** (docs/puml/authentication-flow.puml):
- Vertical layout with detailed steps
- Includes notes about JWT validation
- Legend showing message types
- 12pt fonts, standard arrows

**Presentation** (coding/docs/presentation/puml/authentication-flow.puml):
- Horizontal left-to-right flow
- Only shows: User ‚Üí API ‚Üí Auth ‚Üí DB
- No notes or legends
- 18pt fonts, thick arrows (4pt)
- Labels: "Login", "Validate", "Query" (not "POST /api/v1/auth/login with credentials")

### Important Notes

- **Same filename**: Presentation versions use same name as original (no suffix)
- **Different location**: Stored in coding/docs/presentation/ tree
- **Not versioning**: This is a different presentation format, not a version
- **Reusable**: Presentation mode diagrams in coding/ can be used by all projects
- **Update both**: When updating a diagram, update both standard and presentation if needed

## Automation Opportunities

Consider creating helper scripts for:
- Batch validation of all .puml files
- Automated PNG generation on save
- Pre-commit hooks to enforce naming conventions
- Linting for incremental naming patterns
- Automatic presentation mode conversion

     1‚Üí# Health System
     2‚Üí
     3‚ÜíAutomatic system health monitoring and self-healing that ensures a stable development environment.
     4‚Üí
     5‚Üí## What It Does
     6‚Üí
     7‚ÜíThe Health System provides **failsafe monitoring** with automatic verification and recovery:
     8‚Üí
     9‚Üí- **Pre-Prompt Checks** - Verifies system health before every Claude prompt
    10‚Üí- **Self-Monitoring** - The health system monitors itself
    11‚Üí- **Auto-Healing** - Automatically restarts failed services
    12‚Üí- **Dashboard** - Real-time visualization at `http://localhost:3030`
    13‚Üí
    14‚Üí## Architecture
    15‚Üí
    16‚Üí![Health System Architecture](../images/enhanced-health-monitoring-overview.png)
    17‚Üí
    18‚Üí### Core Components
    19‚Üí
    20‚Üí**1. Health Verifier** (`scripts/health-verifier.js`)
    21‚Üí- Checks databases, services, and processes
    22‚Üí- Generates health scores (0-100) per service
    23‚Üí- Triggers auto-healing when failures detected
    24‚Üí
    25‚Üí**2. Pre-Prompt Hook** (`scripts/health-prompt-hook.js`)
    26‚Üí- Runs automatically before every Claude prompt
    27‚Üí- Returns cached status if fresh (<5 minutes)
    28‚Üí- Spawns async verification if stale
    29‚Üí
    30‚Üí**3. Auto-Healing** (`scripts/health-remediation-actions.js`)

- Integration with Combined Status Line system

#### 3. Global LSL Coordinator (`scripts/global-lsl-coordinator.js`)
- Multi-project session management
- Auto-recovery mechanisms for dead monitors
- Health check coordination across all sessions
- "Plug'n'play" behavior for seamless session management

#### 4. Combined Status Line (`scripts/combined-status-line.js`)
- Unified status display across all Claude Code sessions
- Individual session status with smart abbreviations
- Integration with constraint monitoring and semantic analysis
- Real-time health status updates

## StatusLine Architecture

![StatusLine Architecture](images/statusline-architecture.png)

### Session Discovery Methods
--
1. **Check Combined Status Line**: Verify script is running
2. **Check Health Files**: Ensure health data is being written
3. **Restart Monitoring**: Restart via `coding/bin/coding`

### Health Check Commands

```bash
# Verify all components are working
node scripts/statusline-health-monitor.js --verify

     1‚Üí# Health System
     2‚Üí
     3‚ÜíAutomatic system health monitoring and self-healing that ensures a stable development environment.
     4‚Üí
     5‚Üí## What It Does
     6‚Üí
     7‚ÜíThe Health System provides **failsafe monitoring** with automatic verification and recovery:
     8‚Üí
     9‚Üí- **Pre-Prompt Checks** - Verifies system health before every Claude prompt
    10‚Üí- **Self-Monitoring** - The health system monitors itself
    11‚Üí- **Auto-Healing** - Automatically restarts failed services
    12‚Üí- **Dashboard** - Real-time visualization at `http://localhost:3030`
    13‚Üí
    14‚Üí## Architecture
    15‚Üí
    16‚Üí![Health System Architecture](../images/enhanced-health-monitoring-overview.png)
    17‚Üí
    18‚Üí### Core Components
    19‚Üí
    20‚Üí**1. Health Verifier** (`scripts/health-verifier.js`)
    21‚Üí- Checks databases, services, and processes
    22‚Üí- Generates health scores (0-100) per service
    23‚Üí- Triggers auto-healing when failures detected
    24‚Üí
    25‚Üí**2. Pre-Prompt Hook** (`scripts/health-prompt-hook.js`)
    26‚Üí- Runs automatically before every Claude prompt
    27‚Üí- Returns cached status if fresh (<5 minutes)
    28‚Üí- Spawns async verification if stale
    29‚Üí
    30‚Üí**3. Auto-Healing** (`scripts/health-remediation-actions.js`)
    31‚Üí- Automatic service restart capabilities
    32‚Üí- Database lock cleanup
    33‚Üí- Zombie process termination
    34‚Üí
    35‚Üí**4. Health API** (`integrations/system-health-dashboard/src/dashboard-server.js`)
    36‚Üí- REST API (port 3033) for health <USER_ID_REDACTED>
    37‚Üí- WebSocket for real-time updates
    38‚Üí- Self-monitoring (watches the watchmen)
    39‚Üí
    40‚Üí**5. Dashboard UI** (`integrations/system-health-dashboard/src/dashboard/`)
    41‚Üí- React-based real-time visualization
    42‚Üí- Service status indicators
    43‚Üí- Auto-healing history
    44‚Üí- Manual restart controls
    45‚Üí
    46‚Üí### Multi-Session Architecture
    47‚Üí
    48‚Üí![Multi-Session Health Monitoring](../images/multi-session-health-architecture.png)
    49‚Üí
    50‚ÜíThe health system monitors all active Claude Code sessions:
    51‚Üí- **Per-Project Monitoring**: Each project gets dedicated health tracking
    52‚Üí- **Centralized Dashboard**: Single dashboard shows all projects
    53‚Üí- **Cross-Session Recovery**: Failures in one project don't affect others
    54‚Üí
    55‚Üí## What It Monitors
    56‚Üí
    57‚Üí### Databases
    58‚Üí
    59‚Üí**LevelDB** (`.data/knowledge-graph/`)
    60‚Üí- Lock file detection
    61‚Üí- Integrity checks
    62‚Üí- Write permission verification
    63‚Üí
    64‚Üí**Qdrant** (Vector Database)
    65‚Üí- Service availability (port 6333)
    66‚Üí- Collection health
    67‚Üí- Query performance
    68‚Üí
    69‚Üí**SQLite** (Analytics)
    70‚Üí- Database file accessibility
    71‚Üí- Table integrity
    72‚Üí- Query responsiveness
    73‚Üí
    74‚Üí### Services
    75‚Üí
    76‚Üí**VKB Server** (port 8080)
    77‚Üí- Knowledge visualization service
    78‚Üí- HTTP health endpoint check
    79‚Üí- Auto-restart on failure
    80‚Üí
    81‚Üí**Constraint Monitor** (port 3031)
    82‚Üí- Code <USER_ID_REDACTED> enforcement API
    83‚Üí- Health status reporting
    84‚Üí- Dashboard integration
    85‚Üí
    86‚Üí**Dashboard Server** (port 3030)
    87‚Üí- Health dashboard UI
    88‚Üí- WebSocket server
    89‚Üí- Auto-recovery
    90‚Üí
    91‚Üí**Health API** (port 3033)
    92‚Üí- Self-monitoring API
    93‚Üí- Prevents monitoring system failure
    94‚Üí
    95‚Üí### Processes
    96‚Üí
    97‚Üí- **Stale PID Detection**: Identifies defunct process IDs
    98‚Üí- **Zombie Cleanup**: Removes orphaned processes
    99‚Üí- **Resource Monitoring**: Tracks memory and CPU usage
   100‚Üí
   101‚Üí## How It Works
   102‚Üí
   103‚Üí### Health Verification Flow
   104‚Üí
   105‚Üí![Health Verification Flow](../images/health-verification-flow.png)
   106‚Üí
   107‚Üí**Step-by-Step Process**:
   108‚Üí
   109‚Üí1. **User Issues Prompt**: Claude Code detects user input
   110‚Üí2. **Pre-Prompt Hook Fires**: `health-prompt-hook.js` executes
   111‚Üí3. **Status Check**: Reads `.health/verification-status.json`
   112‚Üí4. **Freshness Test**: Is status < 5 minutes old?
   113‚Üí   - **Yes**: Return cached status immediately (fast path)
   114‚Üí   - **No**: Spawn async verification (background path)
   115‚Üí5. **Background Verification**:
   116‚Üí   - Check all databases
   117‚Üí   - Check all services
   118‚Üí   - Check all processes
   119‚Üí   - Calculate health scores
   120‚Üí   - Trigger auto-healing if needed
   121‚Üí6. **Status Update**: Write new status to `.health/verification-status.json`
   122‚Üí7. **Dashboard Notification**: WebSocket broadcast to dashboard
   123‚Üí
   124‚Üí### Health Check Sequence
   125‚Üí
   126‚Üí![Health Check Sequence](../images/monitoring-health-check-sequence.png)
   127‚Üí
   128‚Üí**Detailed verification sequence**:
   129‚Üí1. Health Verifier starts
   130‚Üí2. Parallel checks for all services
   131‚Üí3. Each service returns health status
   132‚Üí4. Aggregate scoring calculation
   133‚Üí5. Auto-healing decisions
   134‚Üí6. Status file update
   135‚Üí7. Dashboard notification
   136‚Üí
   137‚Üí### Auto-Healing Actions
   138‚Üí
   139‚ÜíWhen failures are detected, the system automatically executes remediation:
   140‚Üí
   141‚Üí**Service Restart Actions**:
   142‚Üí- `restart_vkb_server` - Restart knowledge visualization
   143‚Üí- `restart_constraint_monitor` - Restart code <USER_ID_REDACTED> enforcement
   144‚Üí- `restart_health_api` - Restart health dashboard API
   145‚Üí- `restart_dashboard` - Restart dashboard UI
   146‚Üí
   147‚Üí**Database Recovery Actions**:
   148‚Üí- `clear_leveldb_locks` - Remove stale LevelDB locks
   149‚Üí- `repair_sqlite_database` - Repair corrupted SQLite files
   150‚Üí- `restart_qdrant_connection` - Reconnect to Qdrant
   151‚Üí
   152‚Üí**Process Cleanup Actions**:
   153‚Üí- `kill_zombie_processes` - Clean up orphaned processes
   154‚Üí- `clear_stale_pids` - Remove invalid PID files
   155‚Üí
   156‚Üí### Status File Structure
   157‚Üí
   158‚Üí**Location**: `.health/verification-status.json`
   159‚Üí
   160‚Üí```json
   161‚Üí{
   162‚Üí  "timestamp": "2025-11-16T10:30:00.000Z",
   163‚Üí  "overall_health": 95,
   164‚Üí  "services": {
   165‚Üí    "vkb_server": {
   166‚Üí      "status": "healthy",
   167‚Üí      "score": 100,
   168‚Üí      "last_check": "2025-11-16T10:30:00.000Z"
   169‚Üí    },
   170‚Üí    "constraint_monitor": {
   171‚Üí      "status": "healthy",
   172‚Üí      "score": 100,
   173‚Üí      "last_check": "2025-11-16T10:30:00.000Z"
   174‚Üí    },
   175‚Üí    "leveldb": {
   176‚Üí      "status": "healthy",
   177‚Üí      "score": 100,
   178‚Üí      "last_check": "2025-11-16T10:30:00.000Z"
   179‚Üí    }
   180‚Üí  },
   181‚Üí  "auto_healing": {
   182‚Üí    "last_action": "restart_vkb_server",
   183‚Üí    "timestamp": "2025-11-16T09:15:00.000Z",
   184‚Üí    "success": true
   185‚Üí  }
   186‚Üí}
   187‚Üí```
   188‚Üí
   189‚Üí## Dashboard
   190‚Üí
   191‚Üí![Health Monitor Dashboard](../images/health-monitor.png)
   192‚Üí
   193‚Üí**URL**: `http://localhost:3030`
   194‚Üí
   195‚Üí### Features
   196‚Üí
   197‚Üí**Real-Time Monitoring**:
   198‚Üí- Service status indicators (green/yellow/red)
   199‚Üí- Health scores with trend arrows
   200‚Üí- Last check timestamps
   201‚Üí- Auto-refresh every 5 seconds
   202‚Üí
   203‚Üí**Service Controls**:
   204‚Üí- Manual restart buttons per service
   205‚Üí- Bulk restart all services
   206‚Üí- Enable/disable monitoring
   207‚Üí
   208‚Üí**Auto-Healing History**:
   209‚Üí- Timeline of healing actions
   210‚Üí- Success/failure indicators
   211‚Üí- Action details and logs
   212‚Üí
   213‚Üí**WebSocket Updates**:
   214‚Üí- Live status changes
   215‚Üí- No page refresh needed
   216‚Üí- Sub-second latency
   217‚Üí
   218‚Üí### Starting the Dashboard
   219‚Üí
   220‚Üí```bash
   221‚Üí# Start health dashboard
   222‚Üícd /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/integrations/system-health-dashboard
   223‚ÜíPORT=3030 npm run dashboard
   224‚Üí
   225‚Üí# Dashboard opens at http://localhost:3030
   226‚Üí```
   227‚Üí
   228‚Üí## Configuration
   229‚Üí
   230‚Üí### Health Checks Configuration
   231‚Üí
   232‚Üí**File**: `scripts/health-checks-config.json`
   233‚Üí
   234‚Üí```json
   235‚Üí{
   236‚Üí  "vkb_server": {
   237‚Üí    "enabled": true,
   238‚Üí    "severity": "error",
   239‚Üí    "check_type": "http_health",
   240‚Üí    "endpoint": "http://localhost:8080/health",
   241‚Üí    "auto_heal": true,
   242‚Üí    "auto_heal_action": "restart_vkb_server",
   243‚Üí    "timeout_ms": 5000
   244‚Üí  },
   245‚Üí  "leveldb": {
   246‚Üí    "enabled": true,
   247‚Üí    "severity": "critical",
   248‚Üí    "check_type": "database_health",
   249‚Üí    "path": ".data/knowledge-graph",
   250‚Üí    "auto_heal": true,
   251‚Üí    "auto_heal_action": "clear_leveldb_locks"
   252‚Üí  },
   253‚Üí  "qdrant": {
   254‚Üí    "enabled": true,
   255‚Üí    "severity": "warning",
   256‚Üí    "check_type": "http_health",
   257‚Üí    "endpoint": "http://localhost:6333/health",
   258‚Üí    "auto_heal": false
   259‚Üí  }
   260‚Üí}
   261‚Üí```
   262‚Üí
   263‚Üí**Configuration Options**:
   264‚Üí- `enabled`: Toggle monitoring on/off
   265‚Üí- `severity`: `critical` | `error` | `warning` | `info`
   266‚Üí- `check_type`: `http_health` | `database_health` | `process_health`
   267‚Üí- `auto_heal`: Enable automatic remediation
   268‚Üí- `auto_heal_action`: Name of healing function
   269‚Üí- `timeout_ms`: Check timeout (default: 5000)
   270‚Üí
   271‚Üí## Key Files
   272‚Üí
   273‚Üí**Core System**:
   274‚Üí- `scripts/health-verifier.js` - Main verification logic
   275‚Üí- `scripts/health-prompt-hook.js` - Pre-prompt integration
   276‚Üí- `scripts/health-remediation-actions.js` - Auto-healing actions
   277‚Üí- `scripts/health-checks-config.json` - Service configuration
   278‚Üí- `.health/verification-status.json` - Current health status
   279‚Üí
   280‚Üí**Dashboard**:
   281‚Üí- `integrations/system-health-dashboard/src/dashboard-server.js` - API server
   282‚Üí- `integrations/system-health-dashboard/src/dashboard/` - React UI
   283‚Üí- `integrations/system-health-dashboard/src/components/` - UI components
   284‚Üí
   285‚Üí## Integration
   286‚Üí
   287‚Üí**Related Systems**:
   288‚Üí- [System Health Dashboard](../../integrations/system-health-dashboard/) - Visualization UI
   289‚Üí- [LSL](../lsl/) - Health events logged in session logs
   290‚Üí- [Constraints](../constraints/) - Constraint monitor is a monitored service
   291‚Üí- [Knowledge Management](../knowledge-management/) - Monitors VKB, LevelDB, Qdrant
   292‚Üí
   293‚Üí## Troubleshooting
   294‚Üí
   295‚Üí**Dashboard not loading?**
   296‚Üí```bash
   297‚Üí# Check if API server is running
   298‚Üícurl http://localhost:3033/api/health
   299‚Üí
   300‚Üí# Restart dashboard
   301‚ÜíPORT=3030 npm run dashboard
   302‚Üí```
   303‚Üí
   304‚Üí**Services stuck in unhealthy state?**
   305‚Üí```bash
   306‚Üí# Manually trigger health check
   307‚Üínode scripts/health-verifier.js
   308‚Üí
   309‚Üí# Check verification status
   310‚Üícat .health/verification-status.json | jq '.'
   311‚Üí```
   312‚Üí
   313‚Üí**Auto-healing not working?**
   314‚Üí```bash
   315‚Üí# Check remediation actions log
   316‚Üícat logs/health-remediation.log
   317‚Üí
   318‚Üí# Verify auto_heal is enabled in config
   319‚Üícat scripts/health-checks-config.json | jq '.vkb_server.auto_heal'
   320‚Üí```

46:## StatusLine Architecture
47-
48:![StatusLine Architecture](images/statusline-architecture.png)
49-
50-### Session Discovery Methods
51-
52-The system uses multiple discovery methods to ensure all active sessions are monitored:
53-
54-1. **Registry-based Discovery**: Uses Global LSL Registry for registered sessions
55-2. **Dynamic Discovery**: Scans Claude transcript directories for unregistered sessions
56-3. **Cross-reference Validation**: Verifies monitor processes are alive and healthy
57-4. **Live Transcript Scanning**: Finds sessions regardless of activity age (removed 1-hour filter)
58-
59-**Recent Enhancement**: Removed the 1-hour transcript activity filter to ensure dormant sessions like nano-degree are properly discovered and displayed. The system now shows all sessions with existing transcript monitors, regardless of when they last had activity.
60-
61-### Smart Abbreviation Engine
62-
63-Project names are automatically abbreviated using intelligent algorithms:
64-
65-- **coding** ‚Üí **C**
66-- **curriculum-alignment** ‚Üí **CA** 
67-- **nano-degree** ‚Üí **ND**
68-- **project-management** ‚Üí **PM**
69-- **user-interface** ‚Üí **UI**
70-
71-The algorithm handles:
72-- Single words: First letter (coding ‚Üí C)
73-- Hyphenated words: First letter of each part (curriculum-alignment ‚Üí CA)
74-- Camel case: Capital letters (projectManagement ‚Üí PM)
75-- Multiple separators: Intelligent parsing
76-
77-## Auto-Recovery Mechanisms
78-
79-![Auto-Recovery Flow](images/auto-recovery-flow.png)
80-
81-### Plug'n'Play Behavior
82-
83-The system provides seamless recovery without requiring user intervention:
84-
85-1. **Dead Monitor Detection**: Identifies stale or crashed monitor processes
86-2. **Automatic Recovery**: Spawns new monitors for unmonitored sessions
87-3. **Registry Updates**: Maintains accurate process tracking
88-4. **Health Verification**: Confirms recovery success
89-
90-### Recovery Scenarios
91-
92-- **Stale PID Recovery**: Detects and replaces dead process IDs
93-- **Missing Monitor Recovery**: Creates monitors for active but unmonitored sessions
94-- **Coordinator Recovery**: Restarts coordination processes when needed
95-- **Health Check Recovery**: Resumes health checking when coordinator fails
96-
97-### Global Monitoring Enhancements

**Health Check Trigger**: Pre-prompt hook fires\n2. **Status Collection**:\n   - Read health verification status\n   - Query constraint monitor API\n   - Read trajectory state file\n   - Scan LSL registry\n3. **Status Aggregation**: Combine all indicators\n4. **Display Update**: Update Claude Code status bar\n5. **Cache**: Store for next check\n\n### Update Frequency\n\n**Triggered By**:\n- User prompts (via pre-prompt hook)\n- Health verification completion\n- Trajectory state changes\n- LSL activity events\n\n**Caching**:\n- Health status cached for 5 minutes\n- Constraint compliance cached for 1 minute\n- Trajectory state read on every update\n- LSL status read on every update\n\n### Integration Points\n\n**File Locations**:\n- Health: `.health/verification-status.json`\n- Trajectory: `.specstory/trajectory/live-state.json`\n- LSL Registry: `.lsl/global-registry.json`\n- Constraint API: `http://localhost:3031/api/compliance/:project`\n\n## State Diagrams\n\n### Service Lifecycle States\n\n![Service Lifecycle State](../images/service-lifecycle-state.png)\n\n**Health States**:\n- **Healthy** (Green) - Service operational (score 80-100)\n- **Degraded** (Yellow) - Service impaired (score 50-79)\n- **Unhealthy** (Red) - Service failing (score 0-49)\n- **Unknown** (Gray) - Cannot determine status\n\n**Transitions**:\n- Health check success ‚Üí Healthy\n- Partial failure ‚Üí Degraded\n- Complete failure ‚Üí Unhealthy\n- Check timeout ‚Üí Unknown\n\n### Status Display States\n\n**Color Transitions**:\n- Green ‚Üí <COMPANY_NAME_REDACTED>: 1 hour until session window closes\n- <COMPANY_NAME_REDACTED> ‚Üí Red: Session window has closed\n- Red ‚Üí Green: New session window opened\n\n## Configuration\n\n### Status Line Configuration\n\n**File**: `config/status-line-config.json`\n\n```json\n{\n  \"enabled\": true,\n  \"update_interval_ms\": 5000,\n  \"cache_duration_ms\": 300000,\n  \"health_source\": \".health/verification-status.json\",\n  \"trajectory_source\": \".specstory/trajectory/live-state.json\",\n  \"lsl_registry\": \".lsl/global-registry.json\",\n  \"constraint_api\": \"http://localhost:3031/api/compliance/{project}\",\n  \"abbreviation_style\": \"smart\",\n  \"multi_session_display\": true,\n  \"max_sessions_displayed\": 5\n}\n```\n\n**Configuration Options**:\n- `enabled`: Toggle status line on/off\n- `update_interval_ms`: How often to check for updates (default: 5000ms)\n- `cache_duration_ms`: How long to cache health status (default: 5 minutes)\n- `abbreviation_style`: `smart` | `first-letter` | `full-name`\n- `multi_session_display`: Show multiple sessions or just active one\n- `max_sessions_displayed`: Maximum sessions to show (default: 5)\n\n## Usage\n\n### Starting the Status Line\n\nThe status line is **automatically started** with the `coding` command:\n\n```bash\n# Start Claude Code with status line\ncoding\n\n# Status line updates appear in Claude Code status bar\n```\n\n### Manual Status Line Check\n\n```bash\n# Get current status line output\nnode scripts/combined-status-line.js\n\n# Example output:\n# [üè• 95% | üõ°Ô∏è 94% ‚öôÔ∏è IMP | üìãüü†2130-2230(3min) ‚Üícoding]\n```\n\n### Troubleshooting\n\n**Status line not updating?**\n```bash\n# Check if health verifier is running\nps aux | grep health-verifier\n\n# Manually trigger health check\nnode scripts/health-verifier.js\n\n# Check status files exist\nls -la .health/verification-status.json\nls -la .specstory/trajectory/live-state.json\n```\n\n**Wrong project showing as active?**\n```bash\n# Check LSL registry\ncat .lsl/global-registry.json | jq '.'\n\n# Verify activity timestamps\ncat .lsl/global-registry.json | jq '.sessions[] | {project, last_activity}'\n```\n\n**Abbreviations incorrect?**\n```bash\n# Test abbreviation engine\nnode scripts/combined-status-line.js --test-abbreviations\n\n# Manual abbreviation override in config\n# Edit config/status-line-config.json\n```\n\n## Key Files\n\n**Core System**:\n- `scripts/combined-status-line.js` - Main status line script\n- `scripts/health-verifier.js` - Health status provider\n- `src/live-logging/RealTimeTrajectoryAnalyzer.js` - Trajectory state provider\n- `.lsl/global-registry.json` - LSL session registry\n- `.health/verification-status.json` - Health status cache\n-      1‚Üí@startuml lsl-classification-flow
     2‚Üí!include _standard-style.puml
     3‚Üí
     4‚Üítitle LSL Five-Layer Classification Flow
     5‚Üí
     6‚Üíparticipant "Enhanced\nTranscript Monitor" as monitor
     7‚Üíparticipant "ReliableCoding\nClassifier" as classifier
     8‚Üíparticipant "Session Filter\n(Layer 0)" as session
     9‚Üíparticipant "PathAnalyzer\n(Layer 1)" as path
    10‚Üíparticipant "KeywordMatcher\n(Layer 2)" as keyword
    11‚Üíparticipant "EmbeddingClassifier\n(Layer 3)" as embedding
    12‚Üíparticipant "SemanticAnalyzer\n(Layer 4)" as semantic
    13‚Üíparticipant "LSL File Manager" as filemanager
    14‚Üí
    15‚Üímonitor -> classifier : classify(exchange)
    16‚Üíactivate classifier
    17‚Üí
    18‚Üíclassifier -> session : checkBias(recentHistory)
    19‚Üíactivate session
    20‚Üí
    21‚Üíalt **Strong Bias + Neutral Prompt**
    22‚Üí    session --> classifier : { decision: biasTarget, confidence: 0.72 }
    23‚Üí    note right : Conversation bias\napplied to neutral\nprompt\n<1ms
    24‚Üí    classifier --> monitor : **Decision from Context (Layer 0)**
    25‚Üí    monitor -> filemanager : route based on bias
    26‚Üíelse **No Bias OR Strong Signals**
    27‚Üí    deactivate session
    28‚Üí    classifier -> path : analyzePaths(exchange)
    29‚Üí    activate path
    30‚Üí
    31‚Üí    alt **Direct File Pattern Match**
    32‚Üí        path --> classifier : { isCoding: true, confidence: 0.95 }
    33‚Üí        note right : File operations on\ncoding infrastructure\n<1ms
    34‚Üí        classifier --> monitor : **CODING_INFRASTRUCTURE (Layer 1)**
    35‚Üí        monitor -> filemanager : redirect to coding project
    36‚Üí    else **No File Pattern Match**
    37‚Üí        deactivate path
    38‚Üí        classifier -> keyword : matchKeywords(exchange)
    39‚Üí        activate keyword
    40‚Üí
    41‚Üí        alt **Strong Keyword Match**
    42‚Üí            keyword --> classifier : { isCoding: true, confidence: 0.8 }
    43‚Üí            note right : Clear coding keywords\n<10ms
    44‚Üí            classifier --> monitor : **CODING_INFRASTRUCTURE (Layer 2)**
    45‚Üí            monitor -> filemanager : redirect to coding project
    46‚Üí        else **Weak/No Keyword Match**
    47‚Üí            deactivate keyword
    48‚Üí            classifier -> embedding : classifyByEmbedding(exchange)
    49‚Üí            activate embedding
    50‚Üí
    51‚Üí            alt **High Vector Similarity**
    52‚Üí                embedding --> classifier : { isCoding: true, confidence: 0.85 }
    53‚Üí                note right : Semantic similarity to\ncoding infrastructure\n<3ms
    54‚Üí                classifier --> monitor : **CODING_INFRASTRUCTURE (Layer 3)**
    55‚Üí                monitor -> filemanager : redirect to coding project
    56‚Üí            else **Low Vector Similarity**
    57‚Üí                embedding --> classifier : { isCoding: false, confidence: 0.6 }
    58‚Üí                note right : Definitive negative\nresult
    59‚Üí                classifier --> monitor : **NOT_CODING_INFRASTRUCTURE (Layer 3)**
    60‚Üí                monitor -> filemanager : keep in local project
    61‚Üí            else **Inconclusive Embedding**
    62‚Üí                embedding --> classifier : { isCoding: null, inconclusive: true }
    63‚Üí                deactivate embedding
    64‚Üí                classifier -> semantic : analyzeSemantics(exchange)
    65‚Üí                activate semantic
    66‚Üí                semantic --> classifier : { isCoding: true/false, confidence: 0.7 }
    67‚Üí                note right : LLM deep analysis\n<10ms
    68‚Üí                classifier --> monitor : **Final Decision (Layer 4)**
    69‚Üí                deactivate semantic
    70‚Üí                monitor -> filemanager : route based on decision
    71‚Üí            end
    72‚Üí        end
    73‚Üí    end
    74‚Üíend
    75‚Üí
    76‚Üí' Update bias tracker
    77‚Üíclassifier -> session : addClassification(result)
    78‚Üí
    79‚Üídeactivate classifier
    80‚Üí
    81‚Üínote over classifier
    82‚Üí  **Five-Layer Performance:**
    83‚Üí  ‚Ä¢ Layer 0 (Session): <1ms
    84‚Üí  ‚Ä¢ Layer 1 (Path): <1ms
    85‚Üí  ‚Ä¢ Layer 2 (Keyword): <10ms
    86‚Üí  ‚Ä¢ Layer 3 (Embedding): <3ms
    87‚Üí  ‚Ä¢ Layer 4 (Semantic): <10ms
    88‚Üí  ‚Ä¢ **Total Pipeline: <30ms**
    89‚Üíend note
    90‚Üí
    91‚Üínote over session
    92‚Üí  **Conversation Context:**
    93‚Üí  ‚Ä¢ Sliding window (5 prompts)
    94‚Üí  ‚Ä¢ Temporal decay weighting
    95‚Üí  ‚Ä¢ Bias strength threshold: 0.65
    96‚Üí  ‚Ä¢ Only for neutral prompts
    97‚Üíend note
    98‚Üí
    99‚Üínote over embedding
   100‚Üí  **Vector Similarity Features:**
   101‚Üí  ‚Ä¢ Qdrant vector database
   102‚Üí  ‚Ä¢ 384-dimensional embeddings
   103‚Üí  ‚Ä¢ HNSW indexing + int8 quantization
   104‚Üí  ‚Ä¢ Repository content indexed
   105‚Üí  ‚Ä¢ LRU cache with TTL
   106‚Üíend note
   107‚Üí

## Prompt Set 10 (ps_1763304843962)

**Time:** 2025-11-16T14:54:03.962Z
**Duration:** 1439640423ms

### User

Base directory for this skill: /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/.claude/skills/documentation-style

# Documentation Styling Rules

This skill enforces comprehensive documentation standards across all projects.

## Critical Rules

### 1. NO LINE ART - EVER
**ABSOLUTE RULE**: Never create ASCII art or line-based diagrams in documentation.

**ALWAYS USE**:
- PlantUML for architecture diagrams, sequence diagrams, component diagrams
- Mermaid for flowcharts, state diagrams, simple visualizations

**WHY**: Text-based "line art" is not accessible, difficult to maintain, and looks unprofessional.

### 2. PlantUML Diagram Standards

**Location**: All PlantUML files MUST be stored in `docs/puml/`

**Style Sheet**: ALWAYS include the standard style sheet from coding project as the FIRST line after the opening tag.

**Layout Guidelines**:
- **Standard diagrams**: Prefer VERTICAL layouts to avoid excessive width
- Reason: Prevents users from zooming and scrolling horizontally
- Vertical scrolling is acceptable and preferred over horizontal scrolling
- Aim for narrow, tall diagrams that fit within typical screen widths

**Workflow for Creating PlantUML Diagrams**:

1. **Create the .puml file** in `docs/puml/` with proper naming
2. **Include standard style** - see reference documentation for the exact include syntax
3. **Design with vertical layout** - stack components top-to-bottom when possible
4. **Validate syntax** by attempting to render with plantuml checkonly flag
5. **Fix any errors** reported by plantuml validation
6. **Generate PNG** once error-free using plantuml command
7. **Move PNG to images folder** in docs/images/
8. **Reference in markdown** using relative path to the image

**IMPORTANT**: Never claim success until you've verified the PNG was created without errors.

### 3. Filename Conventions

**STRICT RULES** for ALL documentation artifacts (`.md`, `.puml`, `.png`, etc.):

**Permitted characters**:
- Lowercase letters: `a-z`
- Hyphens: `-`
- Numbers: `0-9`
- Extensions: `.md`, `.puml`, `.png`, etc.

**ONLY permitted exception**: `README.md` (capital letters allowed)

**Good Examples**:
- `system-architecture.puml`
- `deployment-flow.md`
- `api-endpoints.png`
- `README.md` (exception)

**Bad Examples**:
- Capital letters in names
- Underscores instead of hyphens
- CamelCase or PascalCase naming

### 4. NO INCREMENTAL NAMING

**CRITICAL**: Filenames and diagram text MUST represent the CURRENT STATE only, never showing evolution.

**FORBIDDEN PATTERNS** - Never use these suffixes or words:
- Version numbers or indicators
- Words suggesting improvement or change
- Words suggesting temporary status
- Words suggesting alternatives

**Why**: Documentation should reflect current state, not history. Use git for version history.

**Always**: Update the original file directly instead of creating variants.

### 5. Diagram Text Content

Text WITHIN diagrams must also be non-incremental:
- Component names should be simple and current
- Node labels should not indicate versions
- Actor names should not suggest enhancement status

## Implementation Checklist

When creating or updating documentation, verify:

- [ ] No ASCII/line art used (use PlantUML or Mermaid)
- [ ] PlantUML files stored in `docs/puml/`
- [ ] Standard style sheet included in .puml files
- [ ] PlantUML syntax validated with plantuml checkonly
- [ ] PNG generated successfully with plantuml
- [ ] PNG moved to `docs/images/`
- [ ] All filenames use lowercase + hyphens only (except README.md)
- [ ] No incremental suffixes in filenames
- [ ] No incremental labels in diagram text
- [ ] Markdown properly references images from `docs/images/`

## Tool Requirements

**Required tool**: `plantuml` must be installed on the system.

**Verification**:
```bash
which plantuml || echo "ERROR: plantuml not installed"
```

## Error Recovery

If PlantUML generation fails:

1. **Read the error message carefully** - PlantUML errors are usually specific
2. **Check syntax** - common issues include missing tags, unclosed quotes, invalid stereotypes, incorrect arrow syntax
3. **Validate include path** - ensure style sheet path is correct
4. **Test incrementally** - comment out sections to isolate problems

## Project-Specific Paths

### Standard Mode Style Sheet
Located at: `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/docs/puml/_standard-style.puml`

Use this path for regular documentation diagrams (12pt fonts, 2pt lines, vertical layout preference).

### Presentation Mode Style Sheet
Located at: `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/docs/presentation/puml/_standard-style.puml`

Use this path for presentation diagrams (18pt fonts, 3-4pt lines, horizontal layout preference).

**IMPORTANT**: Both style sheets are named `_standard-style.puml` but are in different directories. The constraint monitor requires all PlantUML files to include a file named `_standard-style.puml`, so we use the same name in both locations but with different content optimized for each use case.

## PRESENTATION MODE

### When to Use Presentation Mode

Create a presentation mode version when:
- User explicitly requests "presentation mode" or "PPT version"
- Diagram will be used in PowerPoint or similar presentation software
- Diagram needs to be readable from distance (projector/large screen)
- Focus should be on key concepts, not detailed annotations

### Presentation Mode Workflow

When asked to create a presentation mode version:

1. **Copy source file** from `docs/puml/` to `coding/docs/presentation/puml/`
   - Keep the same filename (no suffix changes)
   - This is stored in coding project for reuse across all projects

2. **Rework the diagram** with these changes:
   - **Thicker lines**: All connections and borders become more prominent
   - **Increased font size**: All text becomes larger (18pt vs 12pt)
   - **Essential text only**: Remove verbose labels, keep only critical identifiers
   - **Remove annotations**: Delete all notes, legends, and explanatory text
   - **Horizontal layout**: Arrange for landscape PPT slide (left-to-right flow)
   - **Simplify**: Focus on core concepts, remove implementation details

3. **Update style sheet include** to presentation style:

   **Absolute path** (when referencing from any project):
   ```
   !include /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/docs/presentation/puml/_standard-style.puml
   ```

   **Relative path** (when file is in the presentation/puml directory):
   ```
   !include _standard-style.puml
   ```

   Note: This is a different `_standard-style.puml` than the regular one - it's the presentation mode version with larger fonts and thicker lines.

4. **Validate and generate**:
   ```bash
   plantuml -checkonly coding/docs/presentation/puml/diagram-name.puml
   plantuml coding/docs/presentation/puml/diagram-name.puml
   mv coding/docs/presentation/puml/diagram-name.png coding/docs/presentation/images/
   ```

5. **Verify** the presentation PNG is created and suitable for PPT use

### Presentation Mode Characteristics

**Differences from Standard Mode**:

| Aspect | Standard Mode | Presentation Mode |
|--------|--------------|-------------------|
| Layout | Vertical (narrow, tall) | Horizontal (wide, landscape) |
| Font Size | 12pt | 18pt |
| Line Thickness | 2pt | 3-4pt |
| Text Detail | Comprehensive | Essential only |
| Annotations | Included | Removed |
| Notes/Legends | Present | Omitted |
| Purpose | Documentation | Presentation |
| Location | `docs/puml/` | `coding/docs/presentation/puml/` |

**Visual Optimization**:
- Thicker borders make elements visible from distance
- Larger fonts readable on projectors
- Horizontal layout fits 16:9 or 4:3 PPT slides
- Minimal text reduces cognitive load
- No legends/notes - slides should be self-explanatory or presenter explains

### Presentation Mode Example

**Original** (docs/puml/authentication-flow.puml):
- Vertical layout with detailed steps
- Includes notes about JWT validation
- Legend showing message types
- 12pt fonts, standard arrows

**Presentation** (coding/docs/presentation/puml/authentication-flow.puml):
- Horizontal left-to-right flow
- Only shows: User ‚Üí API ‚Üí Auth ‚Üí DB
- No notes or legends
- 18pt fonts, thick arrows (4pt)
- Labels: "Login", "Validate", "Query" (not "POST /api/v1/auth/login with credentials")

### Important Notes

- **Same filename**: Presentation versions use same name as original (no suffix)
- **Different location**: Stored in coding/docs/presentation/ tree
- **Not versioning**: This is a different presentation format, not a version
- **Reusable**: Presentation mode diagrams in coding/ can be used by all projects
- **Update both**: When updating a diagram, update both standard and presentation if needed

## Automation Opportunities

Consider creating helper scripts for:
- Batch validation of all .puml files
- Automated PNG generation on save
- Pre-commit hooks to enforce naming conventions
- Linting for incremental naming patterns
- Automatic presentation mode conversion

Based on my investigation of the PlantUML/PNG files, here's what I found:

## ‚úÖ **Good News - System is Well Maintained**

### Layout Direction
**Documentation diagrams (docs/puml/)** are **mostly vertical** as they should be:

- **45 sequence diagrams** - Naturally vertical (no direction needed)
- **71 component diagrams** - Use explicit vertical arrows (`-down->`, `-up->`)
- **6 files** - Have explicit `top to bottom direction` statement
- **Only 2 files** use horizontal layout:
  - `status-line-trajectory-integration.puml` - Appropriate (shows side-by-side system integration)
  - `vkb-cli-use-cases.puml` - Appropriate (use case diagram with actors on left)

**Presentation diagrams (docs/presentation/puml/)** use proper presentation formatting:
- **8 of 17 files** have `left to right direction` (horizontal for slides)
- **Larger fonts** (18pt vs 12pt)
- **Thicker lines** (3pt vs 2pt)
- **Example**: `system-architecture.puml` correctly shows horizontal layout with presentation styling

### PNGs Up to Date
- **117 PUML files** ‚Üí **117 PNG files** (nearly 1:1 match)
- **No PUML files modified** after most recent PNG generation (Nov 16 11:54)
- **Timestamps match** for sampled files (e.g., ukb-architecture: both from Nov 16 11:54)

## ‚ö†Ô∏è **Minor Issues Found**

### Filename Mismatches
Some PUML files have different names than their corresponding PNGs:

| PUML File | PNG File |
|-----------|----------|
| `conversation-based-detection.puml` | `conversation-based-detection-flow.png` |
| `knowledge-flow-sequence.puml` | `knowledge-management-architecture.png` |

Also found:
- `health-monitor.png` exists but no corresponding `.puml` file

### Recommendations

1. **Fix filename mismatches** - Rename either PUML or PNG files to match
2. **Add explicit vertical direction** to the ~38 component diagrams that don't have it (optional but recommended for clarity)
3. **Consider adding horizontal layout** to the 9 presentation diagrams that don't have it explicitly set

**Overall Assessment**: Your PlantUML/PNG files are **in good shape**. The diagrams reflect current system architecture, use appropriate layouts (vertical for docs, horizontal for presentations), and the PNGs are up to date with their source PUML files. The filename mismatches are cosmetic and don't affect functionality.
